• Saved to 01260207201000001250_REGISTRY/ID/gap_closure_verification_report.json.

› these are the files the assesment is based on: "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\gap_closure_verification_report.json"
  "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\# Detailed Solution Document for CL.txt"
  "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\This audit is useful, but it overst.txt"
  "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\artifact_audit_result.json"
  "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\idproblems.md"
  "C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\01260207201000001250_REGISTRY\ID\GOV_REG_REMEDIATION_CLI_INSTRUCTION.md"
  provide feedback on assesment:  Overall Characterization

    The six documents represent three layers of work: an original audit(artifact_audit_result.json), a critique of that
    audit (This audit is useful...), a solution specification (# Detailed Solution Document for CL.txt), a gap
    verification attempt (gap_closure_verification_report.json), and two operational remediation specs
    (GOV_REG_REMEDIATION_CLI_INSTRUCTION.md, idproblems.md).

    The problem is that these layers aren't in sync with each other.

    ---
    What the Gap Closure Report Gets Right

    gap_closure_verification_report.json is a meaningful improvement over artifact_audit_result.json:

    - gaps_truly_closed: [] — zero gaps are claimed closed. That is honest and correct.
    - Every closure_assessment.does_close_gap is false. No false optimism.
    - G5 is classified conflicting rather than partial — that's a real distinction and it's right.
    - The cross_cutting_findings section correctly captures: duplicate/shadow files, registry shape conflicts, identity
    contract conflicts, and missing dependencies.
    - The best_next_files_to_search list is specific and actionable.

    ---
    What the Gap Closure Report Misses

    Problem 1: The gap report doesn't implement the solution document'sschema.

    The solution doc (section 5.1–5.3) defined new vocabulary:
    - candidate_found / implementation_verified / dominant_but_contested / closure_not_proven / missing
    - Split discovery_confidence vs canonicality_confidence
    - Per-candidate execution_verification sub-object: imports_resolve,runtime_exec_verified,
    used_by_dominant_orchestrator, test_reference_found, contract_aligned, duplicate_shadow_absent

    The gap report still uses: partial, missing, conflicting and a single confidence field. None of the
    execution_verification sub-fields exist. The solution document was written, but its schema wasn't applied to the next
    output.

    Problem 2: The final assessment doesn't use the hardened structure.

    The solution doc's section 5.4 defined:
    {
      "has_dominant_runtime_nucleus": ...,
      "has_uncontested_canonical_runtime": ...,
      "has_multiple_competing_orchestrators": ...,
      "orchestrator_integration_verified": ...,
      "has_single_proven_registry_mutation_authority": ...
    }

    The gap report's final_assessment instead has: gaps_truly_closed, gaps_still_open, gaps_blocked_by_conflict,
    best_next_files_to_search. That's useful, but it's a different schema — the original contradiction
    (has_single_canonical_runtime: true with has_single_canonical_orchestrator: false) is not explicitly resolved or
    replaced.

    Problem 3: The two "CLI" documents solve different problems.

    This is easy to miss and important:

    ┌────────────────────────────────────────┬─────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                Document                │      Track      │           Problem solved                    │
    ├────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
    │ GOV_REG_REMEDIATION_CLI_INSTRUCTION.md │ A — File        │ Namingcollisions, duplicate files, dual-ID         │
    │                                        │ Identity        │ filenames, ungoverned files                         │
    ├────────────────────────────────────────┼─────────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
    │ # Detailed Solution Document for       │ B — Runtime     │ Brokenimports, competing implementations, missing  │
    │ CL.txt                                 │ Authority       │ components, single-writer proof                     │
    └────────────────────────────────────────┴─────────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

    Both are real and both are needed, but they are independent. Track A (govreg-remediate) is about cleaning up file
    naming across 163 Python files. Track B is about proving which runtime files are actually authoritative. Nothing in
    the gap report or solution doc acknowledges this distinction explicitly, which risks someone implementing Track A and
    thinking they've addressed Track B.

    Problem 4: Key output files from the solution doc still don't exist.

    Section 14 of the solution doc lists 9 required outputs. None of them have been produced:
    - CANONICAL_AUTHORITY_MAP.json — most important, still absent
    - EXECUTION_VERIFICATION_REPORT.json — absent
    - BLOCKER_REMEDIATION_REPORT.json — absent
    - DUPLICATE_ROLE_ANALYSIS.json — absent
    - etc.

    The gap report is a useful intermediate artifact, but it isn't one of those 9 outputs, and the 9 outputs aren't
    acknowledged as the deliverables yet.

    Problem 5: External files are in the search list but not investigated.

    gap_closure_verification_report.json lists C:\Users\richg\ALL_AI\GOVERNANCE\gates\gate_runner.py and

• Yes.

  The template in newPhasePlanProcess/01260207201000000510_NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3.json and the spec in
  newPhasePlanProcess/01260207201000000180_NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3.json are broad enough to express both:

  - the hardened runtime-authority verification workflow from 01260207201000001250_REGISTRY/ID%23%20Detailed%20Solution%20Document%20for%20CL.txt
  - the Track A file-identity remediation workflow from 01260207201000001250_REGISTRY/ID/GOV_REG_REMEDIATION_CLI_INSTRUCTION.md

  It fits well because the template already supports:

  - step-level contracts with inputs, outputs, invariants, preconditions, postconditions, failure modes, and file scope
  - explicit validation gates and evidence artifacts
  - phase DAGs and parallel execution groups
  - assumption and decision ledgers
  - NOT_AUTOMATABLE escalation for anything that cannot be mechanicallyverified
  - ground-truth levels and artifact-closure checks

  The important adaptation rule is this:

  - use the newPhasePlan template as the execution wrapper
  - keep the solution document’s hardened authority schema as output artifacts produced by the plan, not as replacement top-level template fields

  That means:

  - candidate_found, implementation_verified, dominant_but_contested, closure_not_proven, missing should live inside generated deliverables like
    CANONICAL_AUTHORITY_MAP.json
  - execution_verification should live inside generated verification artifacts, while the plan step itself declares the commands, evidence paths,
    and pass/fail conditions that produce it
  - the hardened final booleans like has_dominant_runtime_nucleus and has_single_proven_registry_mutation_authority should be emitted as final
    deliverable content, and also mirrored in plan success criteria / definition of done

  A clean mapping would be:

  - PH-00 bootstrap and scope freeze
  - PH-01 source corpus intake and file manifest
  - PH-02 external authority resolution
  - PH-03 candidate execution verification
  - PH-04 canonicality adjudication and conflict resolution
  - PH-05 Track A / Track B dependency decision
  - PH-06 remediation-plan correction
  Your specific recommendations map cleanly:

  - Check gate_runner.py and enforcement_bridge.py now:
  - Produce CANONICAL_AUTHORITY_MAP.json:
      - one deliverable-generation step with schema-validation gate
  - Decide whether Track A depends on Track B:
      - one blocking decision step whose output is a decision-ledger artifact

  - template = plan mechanics
  - deliverables = runtime-authority conclusions

  So the answer is yes, with two conditions:

  - Track A and Track B must be represented as separate phase groups with an explicit dependency edge
  - the hardened runtime-authority schemas should be emitted as plannedartifacts, not flattened into generic plan status fields

  If you want, I can generate an actual newPhasePlan JSON for this worknext.
